###xml 591 595 591 595 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL8 </italic>
###xml 674 675 674 675 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 717 721 717 721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL8 </italic>
###xml 772 782 772 782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 810 814 810 814 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL8 </italic>
###xml 903 920 903 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli </italic>
###xml 921 928 921 928 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 921 928 921 928 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>E. coli</italic></bold>
###xml 931 933 931 933 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 979 980 979 980 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 1301 1302 1301 1302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S1">1</xref>
###xml 1364 1366 1364 1366 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 1421 1431 1421 1431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 1432 1434 1432 1434 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 735 741 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 772 781 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 871 877 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 903 919 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 921 928 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1421 1430 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
The chemokine IL8 had the greatest change in expression resulting in a fold-change of 1,054 in infected vs. control quarters (Table S1). The importance of this protein and its related functions was underscored by GO molecular function analysis both when the entire DEG or those with >1.5-fold were analyzed (Additional Files 2 and 15). This chemokine is induced upon stimulation of TNF or IL-1 (Figure 1) and serves as a primary chemoattractant during the innate immune response, thus, playing a major role in the chemotaxis of PMN. Therefore, it seems logical that the dramatic increase in IL8 expression would occur before peak clinical signs of mastitis. Swanson et al. [8] did not observe a significant change in IL8 expression in bovine mammary tissue after IMI with S. uberis (Strain 233); but increased IL8 mRNA expression has been reported in primary isolates of bovine MEC after challenge with Escherichia coli (E. coli) [27]. With regards to results of Swanson et al. [8], mammary tissue was collected between 60-132 hours post-inoculation when peak clinical signs already had occurred. In our study, mammary biopsies were performed prior to peak clinical response and prior to the major influx of PMN into the mammary gland (supported by gene markers analysis, Figure S2 in Additional File 1), milk compositional changes and clinical signs of mastitis [14], and our previous work using this dose and strain of S. uberis [17].
###end p 70
###begin title 71
The anti-inflammatory IL-10 and pro-inflammatory IL-6 pathways are activated before peak clinical signs
###end title 71
###begin p 72
###xml 0 25 0 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Interleukin-10 Signaling </italic>
###xml 97 107 97 107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 114 115 114 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">3</xref>
###xml 120 121 120 121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T4">4</xref>
###xml 130 131 130 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 154 155 154 155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S7">7</xref>
###xml 160 162 160 162 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S12">12</xref>
###xml 251 257 251 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRAF6 </italic>
###xml 310 311 310 311 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 332 334 332 334 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S12">12</xref>
###xml 445 449 445 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL10</italic>
###xml 507 513 507 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAPK12</italic>
###xml 534 535 534 535 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 589 594 589 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL1B </italic>
###xml 625 631 625 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL1R2 </italic>
###xml 783 784 783 784 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 932 940 928 936 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TNF, IL6</italic>
###xml 946 949 942 945 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL1</italic>
###xml 1137 1138 1133 1134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 1183 1189 1179 1185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">STAT3 </italic>
###xml 1247 1253 1243 1249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOCS3 </italic>
###xml 1282 1284 1278 1280 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 1323 1327 1319 1323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL10</italic>
###xml 97 106 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
Interleukin-10 Signaling was among the primary canonical pathways affected by IMI challenge with S. uberis (Table 3 and 4, Figure 1, and Additional Files 7 and 12). The binding of the IL-1 cytokine family to the IL-1 receptor mediates the activity of TRAF6 (tumor necrosis receptor-associated factor 6; Figure 1 and Additional File 12), leading to activation of the p38 MAPK signaling pathway that ultimately leads to increased transcription of IL10. Despite a significant down-regulation of p38 MAPK (i.e. MAPK12; -1.22-fold; Figure 1) during IMI, the observed 13.9-fold up-regulation of IL1B and 38.9-fold up-regulation of IL1R2 probably overcame that response and also might have been sufficient to account for the fact that JAK1 expression was down-regulated (-1.17-fold; Figure 1). Interleukin-10 is an anti-inflammatory cytokine that blocks NF-kappaB activity, which leads to suppression of pro-inflammatory mediators such as TNF, IL6, and IL1. Expression of 22 out of 25 putative components (71 total in IPA) of the IL-10 signaling pathway present in our microarray platform were moderately but significantly up-regulated (Figure 1). Of interest was the mild up-regulation of STAT3 (ca. 3-fold; Table S1) which in turn is known to activate SOCS3 and activate IL-6-signaling [28]. Despite the marked up-regulation of IL10, our results of pathway analysis were indicative of more pronounced inflammation and probably hampered IL-10 anti-inflammatory activity.
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 0 24 0 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Interleukin-6 Signaling </italic>
###xml 75 85 75 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 93 94 93 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">3</xref>
###xml 99 100 99 100 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T4">4</xref>
###xml 112 113 112 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 146 151 146 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL-6 </italic>
###xml 155 170 155 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL-10 Signaling</italic>
###xml 202 233 202 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TNF, IL1B, NFKBIA, STAT3, TRAF6</italic>
###xml 239 243 239 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FOS </italic>
###xml 266 272 266 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MAPK12</italic>
###xml 288 292 288 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL6 </italic>
###xml 444 445 440 441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">2</xref>
###xml 504 509 500 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL-6 </italic>
###xml 513 529 509 525 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL-10 Signaling </italic>
###xml 545 555 541 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 652 675 648 671 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL-6 Signaling Pathway </italic>
###xml 775 798 771 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL-10 Signaling Pathway</italic>
###xml 875 879 871 875 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL6 </italic>
###xml 883 887 879 883 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TNF </italic>
###xml 931 935 927 931 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL10</italic>
###xml 75 84 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 545 554 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
Interleukin-6 Signaling was a major pathway affected by IMI challenge with S. uberis (Tables 3 and 4 and Figure 1). Several genes overlap between IL-6 and IL-10 Signaling, including an up-regulation of TNF, IL1B, NFKBIA, STAT3, TRAF6, and FOS and down-regulation of MAPK12. Expression of IL6 occurs via the NF-kappaB signaling pathway. Interleukin-6 is a pro-inflammatory cytokine that is also involved in acute-phase protein signaling (Figure 2). The coordinated up-regulation of genes involved in both IL-6 and IL-10 Signaling during IMI with S. uberis is suggestive of an ability of the immune system to generate a pro-inflammatory response via the IL-6 Signaling Pathway while attempting to control the severity and duration of the inflammation via the anti-inflammatory IL-10 Signaling Pathway. By far, however, our data suggested that the pro-inflammatory response via IL6 and TNF overrode the anti-inflammatory response via IL10.
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 104 106 101 103 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 107 109 104 106 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 213 214 210 211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 257 264 254 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NFKBIA </italic>
###xml 291 292 288 289 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 378 384 371 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NFKB2 </italic>
###xml 518 520 507 509 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 956 958 945 947 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 987 988 976 977 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">3</xref>
###xml 1087 1088 1076 1077 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">3</xref>
###xml 1107 1108 1096 1097 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S7">7</xref>
###xml 1113 1115 1102 1104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S12">12</xref>
###xml 1221 1223 1210 1212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S15">15</xref>
IL-6 also has been shown to have anti-inflammatory capabilities through inhibition of IL-1beta and TNF [29-31]. In our study, however, the signaling pathway through TNF and IL-1 appeared largely activated (Figure 1), with a more pronounced up-regulation of NFKBIA (in the pathways in Figure 1, IkappaB expression is determined by this gene, which is one of its components) than NFKB2 (this genes is a component of NF-kappaB), which suggested a potential inhibitory effect on the induction of survival genes via NFKB2 [32] and a control of inflammatory response. In the context of regulation of cell death/survival, it was evident that cell survival via enhanced growth and differentiation might have been inhibited due to IMI because the genes coding for phosphorylation enzymes in the ERK (extracellular-regulated kinase)/MAPK (mitogen activated protein kinase) signaling pathway, which is involved in control of a broad range of intracellular functions [33] were down-regulated (Table 3). These data suggested that signaling through phosphorylation (see also PI3K/AKT signaling; Table 3, Additional Files 7 and 12) was inhibited as a result of IMI. This latter finding was also observed by GO analysis (Additional File 15).
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 73 74 73 74 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 113 117 113 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL6 </italic>
###xml 149 154 149 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL10 </italic>
###xml 219 229 219 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 270 271 270 271 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 298 312 298 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus </italic>
###xml 417 442 417 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL1B, IL6, IL8, CD14, FOS</italic>
###xml 448 454 448 454 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NFKBIA</italic>
###xml 636 638 633 635 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 1168 1170 1165 1167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 1258 1268 1255 1265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 191 197 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 219 228 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 1258 1267 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
Our results regarding IL-6 and IL-10 support the work of Swanson et al. [8] who observed an up-regulation of the IL6 receptor (1.83-fold change) and IL10 receptor alpha (1.91-fold change) in bovine mammary tissue after S. uberis IMI. Similar to our data, Lutzow et al. [7] after IMI challenge with Staph. aureus observed an up-regulation (via microarrays) of genes involved in both IL-6 and IL-10 signaling including IL1B, IL6, IL8, CD14, FOS, and NFKBIA. In our study, we isolated whey from all infected quarters and analyzed samples for concentrations of IL-10, IL-1beta, and TNF at 0, 12, and 20 h (time of biopsy) post-inoculation [14]. No significant changes in cytokine concentrations were observed by 20 h post-inoculation when compared to pre-infection levels (0 h). This may be attributed to the fact that the mammary biopsies were performed prior to peak clinical signs of mastitis in order to avoid tissue samples with elevated amounts of mRNA from infiltrating PMN. Unfortunately, the side effects of the biopsy procedure (e.g., blood clots) made it impossible to isolate whey from mammary secretions during peak clinical signs. However, Bannerman et al. [15] evaluated cytokine secretions in whey collected from mammary quarters challenged with S. uberis and observed elevated milk concentrations of IL-1beta, IL-8, IL-10, IL-12, TNF, and IFN-gamma compared with healthy quarters by ~30 h post-challenge.
###end p 75
###begin title 76
Toll-like receptor signaling
###end title 76
###begin p 77
###xml 57 62 57 62 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PAMPs</bold>
###xml 106 109 106 109 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LTA</bold>
###xml 264 272 264 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli </italic>
###xml 473 483 473 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 487 500 487 500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus</italic>
###xml 591 594 591 594 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR</bold>
###xml 678 687 678 687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TNF, IL1B</italic>
###xml 693 696 693 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL6</italic>
###xml 714 717 714 717 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL8</italic>
###xml 800 801 800 801 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">3</xref>
###xml 823 824 823 824 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S6">6</xref>
###xml 826 827 826 827 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S7">7</xref>
###xml 829 830 829 830 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S8">8</xref>
###xml 832 833 832 833 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S9">9</xref>
###xml 838 840 838 840 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S12">12</xref>
###xml 932 974 932 974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR2, TLR4, CASP8, CD14, FOS, IRAK1, TRAF6</italic>
###xml 980 986 980 986 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NFKBIA</italic>
###xml 1046 1053 1046 1053 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TOLLIP </italic>
###xml 1190 1191 1190 1191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 264 271 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 473 482 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
Bacteria contain pathogen-associated molecular patterns (PAMPs) motifs, such as LPS or lipoteichoic acid (LTA), that are potent stimulators of innate immunity. Lipid A is considered the active motif for the PAMP activity of LPS from Gram-negative bacteria such as E. coli that stimulates the innate immune response and activates TLR-4 and the LPS-LPS binding protein-CD14 complex; however, the active motif for the PAMP activity of LTA (i.e. Gram-positive bacteria such as S. uberis and Staph. aureus) remains unknown. Regardless, TLR-2 protein is activated via LTA. The toll-like receptor (TLR) signaling pathway results in the synthesis of several pro-inflammatory cytokines (TNF, IL1B, and IL6) and chemokines (IL8). Although this pathway was not among the most significant in IPA analysis (Table 3 and Additional Files 6, 7, 8, 9 and 12), several genes involved in TLR signaling were up-regulated during IMI challenge including TLR2, TLR4, CASP8, CD14, FOS, IRAK1, TRAF6, and NFKBIA. All genes were verified via qPCR (Table S1). In addition, TOLLIP (toll interacting protein), a negative regulator of inflammation, was also significantly up-regulated (1.15-fold change; Additional File 2).
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 141 155 141 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus </italic>
###xml 156 157 156 157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 158 159 158 159 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 177 178 177 178 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 194 208 194 208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus </italic>
###xml 290 299 290 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR2, FOS</italic>
###xml 305 312 305 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NFKBIA </italic>
###xml 338 352 338 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus </italic>
###xml 363 368 363 368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR4 </italic>
###xml 372 376 372 376 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CD14</italic>
###xml 460 467 460 467 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 558 572 558 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TNF, IL1B, IL8</italic>
###xml 578 582 578 582 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL6 </italic>
###xml 597 610 597 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus</italic>
###xml 634 636 634 636 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
###xml 685 699 685 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus </italic>
###xml 795 799 791 795 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TNF </italic>
###xml 803 808 799 804 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CXCL8</italic>
###xml 909 922 905 918 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus</italic>
###xml 949 963 945 959 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus </italic>
###xml 1042 1044 1034 1036 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
###xml 1291 1293 1279 1281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
###xml 1357 1362 1345 1350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BNBD5</italic>
###xml 1506 1507 1494 1495 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 1510 1511 1498 1499 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 1560 1562 1548 1550 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 1700 1709 1688 1697 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis</italic>
###xml 460 467 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1700 1709 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
Several studies have evaluated gene expression profiles in mammary tissue or MEC lines after challenge with another Gram-positive bacterium, Staph. aureus [6,7]. Lutzow et al. [7] observed that Staph. aureus alters both TLR-2 and TLR-4 signaling pathways. They observed an up-regulation of TLR2, FOS, and NFKBIA during IMI challenge with Staph. aureus as well as TLR4 and CD14, both of which are primarily activated via LPS from Gram-negative bacteria such as E. coli. These researchers also observed an up-regulation of pro-inflammatory mediators including TNF, IL1B, IL8, and IL6 after IMI with Staph. aureus. However, Yang et al. [26] observed that IMI challenge with high doses of Staph. aureus (10,000 cfu; Strain 1027) failed to activate NF-kappaB signaling and the pro-inflammatory genes TNF and CXCL8. A "weak" immune response may be attributed to the virulence factors associated with this strain of Staph. aureus, because heat-inactivated Staph. aureus increased the expression of TLR signaling components and NF-kappaB activation [26]. The TLR-mediated NF-kappaB activation not only signals numerous pro-inflammatory genes but also other anti-microbial immune defense genes such as beta-defensins, which are oxygen-independent peptides that have potent anti-microbial activities [34]. Our data also showed a significant increase in expression of BNBD5, the most abundantly-expressed member of the beta-defensin family of bactericidal peptides in MEC (4.19-fold change; Table S1; Additional File 2) [6]. Our data support results from Swanson et al. [35], who found increased expression of lingual antimicrobial peptide (LAP), a member of the beta-defensin family, during IMI challenge with S. uberis.
###end p 78
###begin p 79
###xml 69 74 69 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR2 </italic>
###xml 78 83 78 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR4 </italic>
###xml 108 118 108 118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 175 176 175 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 207 212 207 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR2 </italic>
###xml 220 225 220 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR4 </italic>
###xml 267 277 267 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 311 316 311 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR2 </italic>
###xml 320 325 320 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR4 </italic>
###xml 447 448 447 448 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 449 451 449 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
###xml 452 454 452 454 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 532 540 532 540 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli </italic>
###xml 543 556 543 556 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus</italic>
###xml 645 646 645 646 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 689 694 689 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR2 </italic>
###xml 698 703 698 703 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR4 </italic>
###xml 776 786 776 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. aureus </italic>
###xml 875 877 875 877 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
###xml 891 896 891 896 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR2 </italic>
###xml 900 905 900 905 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR4 </italic>
###xml 955 969 955 969 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus </italic>
###xml 972 979 972 979 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1058 1060 1058 1060 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 1117 1131 1117 1131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Staph. aureus </italic>
###xml 1161 1162 1161 1162 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 108 117 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 239 245 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 267 276 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 532 539 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 728 734 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 776 785 <span type="species:ncbi:1280">S. aureus</span>
###xml 972 979 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1021 1027 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
Our microarray analysis demonstrated an increased expression of both TLR2 and TLR4 after IMI challenge with S. uberis compared with control quarters. However, Swanson et al. [8] observed an up-regulation of TLR2 but not TLR4 expression in bovine mammary tissue after S. uberis IMI. Increased expression of both TLR2 and TLR4 signaling pathways during IMI challenge with Gram-positive or Gram-negative bacteria has been observed in recent studies [7,26,36]. Most of these studies have examined TLR expression patterns in response to E. coli or Staph. aureus, both major pathogens associated with mastitis in the dairy industry. Goldammer et al. [6] reported an increased expression of both TLR2 and TLR4 (8-to-12-fold change) in bovine mammary quarters naturally infected with S. aureus when compared to healthy quarters. This response is supported by results of Yang et al. [26], where both TLR2 and TLR4 were up-regulated after IMI challenge with either Staph. aureus or E. coli. Similar results were also observed when bovine MEC were challenged with LPS [36], as well as in mammary tissue after IMI challenge with Staph. aureus (determined via microarrays) [7].
###end p 79
###begin title 80
Other DEG involved with immune response
###end title 80
###begin p 81
###xml 85 95 85 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 104 112 104 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-DRA </italic>
###xml 159 160 159 160 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S1">1</xref>
###xml 178 179 178 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 185 190 185 190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C1QC </italic>
###xml 237 238 237 238 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S1">1</xref>
###xml 256 257 256 257 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 260 268 260 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-DRA </italic>
###xml 324 330 324 330 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MHC II</bold>
###xml 473 475 473 475 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 547 549 547 549 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 695 704 695 704 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis</italic>
###xml 781 782 781 782 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 813 821 813 821 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-DRA </italic>
###xml 871 881 871 881 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 1054 1057 1054 1057 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CD4</italic>
###xml 1193 1201 1193 1201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HLA-DRA </italic>
###xml 1397 1402 1397 1402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C1QC </italic>
###xml 1452 1453 1452 1453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 1507 1517 1507 1517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 1550 1552 1550 1552 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 1662 1666 1662 1666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C1qA</italic>
###xml 1668 1678 1668 1678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C1qB, C1s </italic>
###xml 1682 1685 1682 1685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C1r</italic>
###xml 1722 1729 1722 1729 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1848 1850 1848 1850 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 2049 2051 2049 2051 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 85 94 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 695 704 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 843 849 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 871 880 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 1507 1516 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 1690 1696 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 1722 1729 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Other DEG of interest that were significantly up-regulated during IMI challenge with S. uberis included HLA-DRA (1.82-fold change; Table S1 in Additional File 1; Additional File 2) and C1QC (1.37-fold change; Table S1 in Additional File 1; Additional File 2). HLA-DRA codes for the major histocompatability complex type II (MHC II) DR alpha and is primarily expressed on T lymphocytes and macrophages. This gene is considered a candidate gene marker of disease resistance [37]. The role of MHC II in mammary tissue is unclear. Fitzpatrick et al. [38]observed expression of MHC II-positive cells in the connective tissue of the healthy mammary quarters and quarters infected with formalin-killed S. uberis; although individual cell identification was not conducted. Swanson et al. [8] reported an up-regulation of HLA-DRA (1.73-fold change) in bovine mammary tissue after S. uberis IMI. The MHC II complex presents antigen fragments to T-helper cells by binding to the CD4 receptor on T-helper cells. However, we did not detect differential expression of CD4. Although mammary tissue was thoroughly blotted with gauze to remove any visual milk secretions, it is possible that the expression of HLA-DRA may have been acquired through milk lymphocytes and macrophages present in mammary tissue during the biopsy. MHC II expression in MEC warrants further investigation. The observed up-regulation of C1QC was opposite to results from both Swanson et al. [8] who found down-regulation (-1.74-fold change) after S. uberis IMI and those of Gunther et al. [27] who observed a 1.6 to 3.2-fold decrease in mRNA expression of factors associated with the C1 complex (e.g., C1qA, C1qB, C1s and C1r) in bovine MEC after challenge with E. coli. The complement component C1q is the first step in the initiation of the classical pathway of the complement cascade [39]. Researchers have not been able to quantify C1q concentrations in mastitic milk and primarily attribute this to its large size (900 kDa), which may render it impermeable to the mammary epithelium [40].
###end p 81
###begin p 82
###xml 274 276 274 276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 372 374 372 374 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C3</bold>
###xml 422 425 422 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C3 </italic>
###xml 535 545 535 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 586 587 586 587 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 645 647 645 647 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 535 544 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 845 848 <span type="species:ncbi:37162?0.34174508126603936">MAC</span>
No current information is available on the use of the lectin pathway in the mammary gland during an IMI. Researchers have concluded that the mammary gland must lack the classical pathway and therefore must rely primarily on the alternative pathway of the complement system [39]. The initial step of the alternative pathway involves the cleavage of complement component 3 (C3) into fragments C3a and C3b. The expression of C3 (via microarray and qPCR) was significantly up-regulated (1.43-fold change) in mammary quarters infected with S. uberis and supports the work of Swanson et al. [8]. The C3 component has been quantified in mastitic milk [41]. C3 is also a downstream intermediate step involved with both the classical and alternative pathways of the complement system that ultimately leads to the assembly of the membrane attack complex (MAC complex), which consists of complement proteins C5a, C6, C7, C8, and C9. The membrane attack complex plays a role in the disruption of the bacteria cell walls during the immune response.
###end p 82
###begin p 83
###xml 158 163 158 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CD59 </italic>
###xml 186 191 186 191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CD55 </italic>
###xml 227 228 227 228 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 231 236 231 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CD59 </italic>
###xml 314 318 314 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CD55</italic>
###xml 750 755 750 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C1QC </italic>
###xml 796 805 796 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis</italic>
###xml 823 824 823 824 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 867 871 867 871 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C1Q </italic>
###xml 934 944 934 944 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 1047 1050 1047 1050 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C3 </italic>
###xml 1054 1057 1054 1057 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C1Q</italic>
###xml 796 805 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
###xml 934 943 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
Two genes involved in inhibition of the complement cascade were significantly up-regulated in infected versus non-infected mammary quarters. These genes were CD59 (1.22-fold change) and CD55 (2.07-fold change) (Additional File 2). CD59 is involved in the inhibition of the assembly of the membrane attack complex. CD55, or the decay accelerating factor for complement, binds to both the C2-C4b complex of the classical pathway and the C3-Cfb complex of the alternative pathway. This binding accelerates their decay, disrupting the cleavage of C3 into C3b and C3a fragments, which leads to inhibition of the cascade and prevention of damage to host cells. To our knowledge, this is the first report of a significant up-regulation in expression of the C1QC gene from mammary quarters infected with S. uberis. Swanson et al. [8] observed an inverse relationship between C1Q expression (-1.74-fold change) and C3 (2.36-fold change) after S. uberis IMI. The researchers did not elaborate on the inverse relationship in gene expression patterns between C3 and C1Q. Further research related to the classical pathway of the complement cascade in the mammary gland is needed.
###end p 83
###begin title 84
Cell proliferation, angiogenesis, and apoptosis
###end title 84
###begin p 85
###xml 309 311 309 311 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3B</xref>
###xml 341 342 341 342 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">3</xref>
###xml 419 420 419 420 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S7">7</xref>
###xml 425 426 425 426 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S9">9</xref>
###xml 475 479 475 479 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PDGF</bold>
The overall functional analysis both in IPA and GO clearly indicated an induction of proliferation of several types of cells but in particular immune, endothelial, and muscle cells. In contrast, several significantly-enriched pathways related to proliferation/angiogenesis were strongly (e.g., IGF1 in Figure 3B and ephrin receptor in Table 3) or likely inhibited (Aryl Hydrocarbon Receptor signaling; Additional Files 7 and 9), with both the platelet-derived growth factor (PDGF) and PI3K/AKT signaling pathways likely induced (see below).
###end p 85
###begin title 86
Angiogenesis and inflammation: possible role of PDGF signaling and hypoxia
###end title 86
###begin p 87
###xml 32 36 32 36 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PDGF</bold>
###xml 164 166 164 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 461 463 461 463 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 815 817 815 817 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 1025 1027 1025 1027 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S15">15</xref>
###xml 1032 1034 1032 1034 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S16">16</xref>
###xml 1163 1164 1163 1164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">3</xref>
###xml 1207 1209 1207 1209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B43">43</xref>
Platelet-derived growth factor (PDGF) refers to a family of dimeric isoforms that are important for growth, survival, and function especially in connective tissue [42]. Four different PDGF chains have been identified, the classical PDGF-A and PDGF-B and the more recent PDGF-C and PDGF-D isoforms. These isoforms that occur as homodimers or heterodimers (PDGF-AA, AB, BB, CC and DD) exert their effects by differential binding to two receptor tyrosine kinases [42]. Binding of PDGF induces dimerization and autophosphorylation of the tyrosine kinase receptors. Depending on the PDGF isoform involved, homo or heterodimers of the receptor are formed. It is interesting that paracrine PDGF-B signaling has a role in blood vessel formation (i.e., angiogenesis) and it is a potent effector of epithelial cancer growth [42]. The likely induction of PDGF pathway in our study might partly explain the induction of biological processes such as positive regulation of cell proliferation and vasculature development (Additional Files 15 and 16). In fact, signaling through PDGF might have counteracted the marked inhibition of the Ephrin receptor signaling pathway (Table 3), which also is a pro-angiogenic pathway [43].
###end p 87
###begin p 88
###xml 109 111 109 111 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B43">43</xref>
###xml 355 360 355 360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIF1A</italic>
###xml 412 413 412 413 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 521 526 521 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIF1B</italic>
###xml 529 531 529 531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B43">43</xref>
###xml 838 840 838 840 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B43">43</xref>
###xml 947 949 947 949 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
###xml 957 963 957 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIF1A </italic>
###xml 1031 1037 1031 1037 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SLC2A3</italic>
###xml 1039 1044 1039 1044 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAPDH</italic>
###xml 1046 1050 1046 1050 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LDHA</italic>
###xml 1085 1088 1085 1088 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL6</italic>
###xml 1090 1093 1090 1093 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL8</italic>
###xml 1095 1100 1095 1100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PDGFB</italic>
###xml 1147 1152 1147 1152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMOX1</italic>
###xml 1154 1157 1154 1157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LTF</italic>
###xml 1263 1266 1263 1266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FOS</italic>
###xml 1268 1272 1268 1272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">JUNB</italic>
###xml 1301 1302 1301 1302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 1424 1426 1424 1426 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
###xml 1510 1517 1510 1517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SLC2A3 </italic>
###xml 1645 1651 1645 1651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LALBA </italic>
###xml 1903 1904 1903 1904 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S6">6</xref>
A key factor contributing to angiogenesis and aberrant cellular growth (e.g., epithelial tumors) is hypoxia [43]. As cells outgrow their blood supply or are deprived of oxygen, a transcriptional response to hypoxia is initiated. Although several transcription factor pathways seem to be involved, most attention has focused on hypoxia-inducible factor 1 (HIF1A), which was up-regulated with IMI (Additional File 2). This is a heterodimer of two DNA binding proteins, HIF1A, and the aryl hydrocarbon nuclear translocator (HIF1B) [43]. In normoxia, HIF1A is unstable and rapidly degrades via the proteasome, but as oxygen tension drops below 2% (e.g., air is <20%), HIF1A is stabilized, translocates to the nucleus and interacts with HIF1B. The heterodimer initiate a complex transcriptional program via specific hypoxia response elements [43]. In our experiment, we observed up-regulation of many hypoxia-responsive genes as seen in non-ruminants [44], e.g. HIF1A and several others involved in glucose metabolism/glycolysis (e.g., SLC2A3, GAPDH, LDHA), growth factors/cytokines (e.g., IL6, IL8, PDGFB), oxygen transport and iron metabolism (e.g., HMOX1, LTF), as well as several other genes/transcription factors involved in wound healing and angiogenesis (e.g., FOS, JUNB) (Table S1; Additional File 2). It is also interesting that both pyruvate and lactate originating from anaerobic glycolysis in tissues are angiogenic [44]. In the context of our study, a greater uptake of glucose due to up-regulation of SLC2A3 coupled with a reduction in the need for TAG synthesis as well as lactose for secretion in milk (e.g., most lipogenic genes and LALBA were down-regulated) could have led to accumulation of pyruvate from glycolysis and might have played a role in promoting hypoxia. The accumulation of pyruvate seems to be supported also by the likely inhibition of pyruvate metabolism (Additional File 6).
###end p 88
###begin p 89
###xml 25 31 25 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HIF1A </italic>
###xml 62 65 62 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">AHR</italic>
###xml 265 266 265 266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T3">3</xref>
###xml 378 382 378 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL6 </italic>
###xml 400 407 400 407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NFKBIA </italic>
###xml 424 425 424 425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
Despite up-regulation of HIF1A and aryl hydrocarbon receptor (AHR) due to IMI, our pathway analysis revealed that the two signaling pathways associated with response to hypoxia (Ephrin receptor and Aryl hydrocarbon receptor) were for the most part inhibited (Table 3). In the case of the Aryl hydrocarbon receptor signaling pathway, it seems likely that the marked increases in IL6 and activation of NFKBIA (Additional File 2) were the main causes for overall inhibition of the pathway.
###end p 89
###begin title 90
The mystery of IGF1 signaling and inflammation
###end title 90
###begin p 91
###xml 38 42 38 42 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IGF1</bold>
###xml 127 129 127 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 224 226 224 226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 322 328 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 469 475 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
Insulin-like growth factor binding 1 (IGF1) is considered an anabolic hormone and plays a pivotal role in mammary development [45] and potentially in maintaining the epithelial cells during the declining phase of lactation [46]. However, there is no evidence of a role of IGF1 in lactating mammary tissue, at the least in bovine. In support of this, work from one of our laboratories has observed that IGF1 signaling is not among the significantly affected pathways in bovine mammary tissue during lactation and appeared to be inhibited (M. Bionaz, S. L. Rodriguez-Zas, R. E. Everts, H. A. Lewin, and J. J. Loor, University of Illinois, Urbana, unpublished results).
###end p 91
###begin p 92
###xml 35 37 35 37 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3B</xref>
###xml 55 56 55 56 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S7">7</xref>
###xml 87 97 87 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. uberis </italic>
###xml 347 349 347 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B47">47</xref>
###xml 632 634 632 634 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S15">15</xref>
###xml 779 781 779 781 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S15">15</xref>
###xml 847 849 847 849 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S15">15</xref>
###xml 87 96 <span type="species:ncbi:1349">S. uberis</span>
The IGF1 signaling pathway (Figure 3B; Additional File 7) was strongly inhibited after S. uberis challenge, suggesting "resistance" of mammary tissue to IGF1 during IMI. In the immune system, signaling via IGF1 is a crucial event resulting in postponement of apoptosis (increasing survival) of PMN through mediation of the PI3K signaling pathway [47]. If that holds true in mammary after IMI, our data suggest that apoptosis of PMN was probably substantial at 20 h post inoculation. The functional analysis in IPA indicated that apoptosis was significantly affected, with a balance between induction and inhibition (Additional File 15) but overall this process was likely induced particularly in macrophages (Figure S2). Furthermore, as indicated by GO analysis (Additional File 15), apoptosis occurred through caspase activation (Additional File 15).
###end p 92
###begin p 93
###xml 196 198 196 198 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B48">48</xref>
###xml 397 399 397 399 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 355 359 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">cows</span>
###xml 663 669 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
To our knowledge a direct inhibitory effect of inflammation on IGF1 signaling has not been reported; however, modulation of IGF signaling by glucocorticoids in muscle was previously demonstrated [48]. This observation suggests a possible effect of corticoids prior to mammary tissue collection. However, plasma cortisol was not increased significantly in cows after IMI in the present experiment [14]. In summary, the inhibition of IGF1 signaling might have played a role in decreased immune cell survival, particularly macrophages. A possible inhibitory effect of glucocorticoids on this pathway cannot be excluded. The inhibition of IGF1 signaling after IMI in bovine mammary is a novel finding that still requires teleological explanation.
###end p 93
###begin title 94
Lipid metabolism and immune response
###end title 94
###begin title 95
Integration of lipid metabolism and inflammation: possible role of LXR/RXR and PPAR signaling pathways
###end title 95
###begin p 96
###xml 92 94 92 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B49">49</xref>
###xml 95 97 95 97 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B50">50</xref>
###xml 100 106 100 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARA </italic>
###xml 227 229 227 229 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B49">49</xref>
###xml 253 258 249 254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARG</italic>
###xml 352 354 348 350 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B50">50</xref>
###xml 355 357 351 353 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 481 483 473 475 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 486 492 478 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARA </italic>
###xml 496 502 488 494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARG </italic>
###xml 537 539 529 531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B50">50</xref>
###xml 540 542 532 534 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B52">52</xref>
###xml 545 551 537 543 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARG </italic>
###xml 673 675 661 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 405 411 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
Both LXRs and PPARs are involved in the regulation of metabolic and inflammatory signaling [49,50]. PPARA is expressed in liver, brown adipose tissue, heart, and muscle tissue and plays a pivotal role in fatty acid catabolism [49]; whereas, PPAR-gamma (PPARG) is highly expressed in adipose tissue and macrophages and primarily regulates adipogenesis [50,51]. PPAR-gamma has been shown to be expressed in bovine mammary tissue and is also significantly increased during lactation [51]. PPARA and PPARG have anti-inflammatory properties [50,52]. PPARG has been shown to interfere with the transcription of pro-inflammatory factors such as STAT and NF-kappaB in macrophages [53].
###end p 96
###begin p 97
###xml 134 136 134 136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B54">54</xref>
###xml 183 188 183 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR4 </italic>
###xml 238 240 238 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 445 447 445 447 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B56">56</xref>
###xml 613 616 613 616 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LPS</bold>
###xml 649 651 646 648 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 882 886 876 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL6 </italic>
###xml 898 902 892 896 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TNF </italic>
###xml 913 918 907 912 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IL1B </italic>
###xml 933 938 927 932 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CCL2 </italic>
###xml 995 1001 989 995 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NOS2A </italic>
###xml 1016 1021 1010 1015 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MMP7 </italic>
###xml 1061 1062 1055 1056 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 1255 1257 1249 1251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 1290 1296 1284 1290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NOS2A </italic>
###xml 1422 1426 1416 1420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eNOS</italic>
###xml 1443 1447 1437 1441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">iNOS</italic>
###xml 1490 1492 1484 1486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B58">58</xref>
###xml 1506 1508 1500 1502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B59">59</xref>
###xml 1546 1551 1540 1545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR4 </italic>
###xml 1674 1679 1668 1673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TLR4 </italic>
###xml 1732 1737 1726 1731 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">IRF6 </italic>
###xml 1754 1755 1748 1749 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 1758 1760 1752 1754 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 1483 1488 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1498 1504 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
In non-ruminant macrophages, studies have shown that ligand-activated LXR inhibits expression of genes involved with immune response [54]. Interestingly, studies have also shown that TLR4 activation in macrophages inhibits LXR signaling [55]. Activation of inflammatory signaling pathways and release of inflammatory mediators are fundamental to the diverse immune functions of macrophages, and the mammary gland possesses resident macrophages [56]. In addition to inducing genes involved in reverse cholesterol transport, LXR reciprocally represses a set of inflammatory genes after bacterial lipopolysacharide (LPS), TNF, or IL-1beta stimulation [57]. Examples of such genes include those involved in generation of bioactive molecules such as NOS2A, IL-6, TNF, and IL-1beta, the chemokines CCL2, and matrix metallopeptidases. We found that IMI resulted in marked up-regulation of IL6 (430-fold), TNF (45-fold), IL1B (14-fold), and CCL2 (3.3-fold) and moderate but significant up-regulation of NOS2A (1.2-fold) and MMP7 (1.4-fold; Table S1 and Additional File 2). As previously stated, most of the responses in the present study are likely attributed to MEC and potentially resident macrophages, which constitute ca. 5% or more of the parenchyma tissue [18]. It is possible that increased NOS2A expression may be attributed to resident macrophages. However, studies have reported increased expression of the endothelial (eNOS) and inducible (iNOS) forms of nitric oxide synthase in human [58] and murine [59] breast cancer tissue. The increased TLR4 expression after IMI in our study may partly explain the down-regulation of the genes involved with LXR/RXR signaling. The TLR4 response might have been driven via up-regulation of IRF6 (Additional File 2) [57].
###end p 97
###begin p 98
###xml 221 223 221 223 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B60">60</xref>
###xml 257 259 257 259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B60">60</xref>
###xml 456 461 453 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NR1H2</italic>
###xml 610 616 607 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SREBF1</italic>
###xml 625 631 622 628 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SREBF2</italic>
###xml 166 172 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 226 231 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mouse</span>
Studies investigating the LXR/RXR signaling pathway in the mammary gland are sparse and have primarily focused on expression of genes involved in this pathway during murine lactation regardless of bacteriological status [60]. Mouse mammary microarray data [60] has suggested the potential involvement of two systems in controlling fatty acid metabolism. These include the LXR/RXR pathway controlling 1) beta-oxidation of fatty acids via LXR (also known as NR1H2)/PPAR dimers; and 2) fatty acid synthesis involving the LXR/RXR dimer, which induce expression of the sterol regulatory element-binding proteins 1 (SREBF1) and 2 (SREBF2).
###end p 98
###begin p 99
###xml 106 108 106 108 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
###xml 265 267 265 267 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 14 20 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 143 149 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 304 310 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 719 725 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
The lactating bovine mammary gland does not seem to oxidize long-chain fatty acids as a source of energy [61], thus, any involvement of LXR in bovine mammary tissue might be at the level of fatty acid synthesis and/or inflammation (as in non-ruminant macrophages) [57]. However, the expression of LXR in bovine mammary tissue only increased slightly during lactation relative to pregnancy and it was not among DEG (M. Bionaz, S. L. Rodriguez-Zas, R. E. Everts, H. A. Lewin, and J. J. Loor, University of Illinois, Urbana, unpublished results). Those responses coupled with the lack of change in LXR expression due to IMI were suggestive of a minor role for LXR in mediating anti-inflammatory or lipogenic mechanisms in bovine mammary tissue.
###end p 99
###begin p 100
###xml 14 20 14 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARA </italic>
###xml 336 342 336 342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARG </italic>
###xml 450 452 450 452 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 465 471 465 471 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARG </italic>
###xml 768 772 764 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CD36</italic>
###xml 803 822 799 818 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACACA, FASN, SREBF1</italic>
###xml 850 860 846 856 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">LPIN1, SCD</italic>
###xml 863 865 859 861 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B62">62</xref>
###xml 1108 1110 1100 1102 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B63">63</xref>
###xml 1113 1118 1105 1110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARG</italic>
###xml 1184 1191 1176 1183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ALOX5AP</italic>
###xml 1308 1314 1300 1306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PPARG </italic>
###xml 1343 1351 1335 1343 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ALOX5AP </italic>
###xml 1713 1715 1701 1703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B64">64</xref>
###xml 1740 1748 1728 1736 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ALOX5AP </italic>
###xml 1784 1792 1772 1780 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli </italic>
###xml 1863 1871 1851 1859 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ALOX5AP </italic>
###xml 1886 1888 1874 1876 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 44 50 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 260 266 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 485 491 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 596 602 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 961 965 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1128 1132 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1784 1791 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Expression of PPARA is barely detectable in bovine mammary tissue (M. Bionaz, S. L. Rodriguez-Zas, R. E. Everts, H. A. Lewin, and J. J. Loor, unpublished results) and tends to decrease during lactation, which points to a minor role of this nuclear receptor in bovine mammary lipid metabolism. We recently showed that mRNA expression of PPARG was consistently up-regulated during lactation, suggesting that it could play a role in milk fat synthesis [51]. A role of PPARG in regulating bovine milk fat synthesis machinery was supported by recent results we obtained where treatment of MacT cells (bovine mammary epithelial immortalized cells) with rosiglitazone, a specific PPARgamma agonist, resulted in coordinated up-regulation of genes involved in FA import (e.g., CD36), de novo FA synthesis (e.g., ACACA, FASN, SREBF1), and TAG synthesis (e.g., LPIN1, SCD) [62]. More importantly in the context of the present study, a recent study with PPARgamma-knockout mice indicated that its absence increased utilization of long-chain fatty acids for synthesis of inflammatory lipids due to reduced TAG synthesis [63]. PPARG-knockout mice had a sustained increase in 12-lipoxygenase (i.e., ALOX5AP) activity from parturition through the end of lactation. Although we did not observe a significant effect of IMI on PPARG expression, up-regulation of ALOX5AP (ca. 6-fold; Table S1) might have been associated with increased synthesis of eicosanoids which are classical effectors of an inflammatory response. In addition, activation of PPARgamma by specific agonists reduced synthesis of inflammatory cytokines in mammary epithelial cells, suggesting this nuclear receptor has an anti-inflammatory role in mammary tissue [64]. A 39-fold increase of ALOX5AP in mammary quarters challenged with E. coli in a recent study provides further support to the inflammatory role of ALOX5AP during an IMI [27].
###end p 100
###begin p 101
###xml 375 376 363 364 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4</xref>
###xml 493 499 473 479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">INSIG1</italic>
###xml 665 667 641 643 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B62">62</xref>
###xml 756 763 732 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">INSIG1 </italic>
###xml 902 909 874 881 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SREBF1 </italic>
###xml 913 920 885 892 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SREBF2 </italic>
###xml 1090 1095 1062 1067 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACACA</italic>
###xml 1122 1126 1094 1098 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FASN</italic>
###xml 1129 1131 1101 1103 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 1462 1463 1418 1419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4</xref>
###xml 632 638 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 968 974 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
